Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you see the cauterization, prepare yourself if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we said in the division, and do not hesitate or lose hope, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, therefore I perform the cauterization on the head of the chief:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I emme the head of the chief, and the other towards the front at the end of the cuts:
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and it touches the two horns, and it behind the hump:
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and so much of your hand that the cauterization lives on the bone, and so much that the pus comes out forcefully, as if the vapors of the large humors can come out:
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and the cauterization is done on mice according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the burning is everywhere sparse.
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	And if the burning is manifested, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these burns that we have mentioned or chief, and I cauterize in one go, and II cauterizes on the point of the shoulder, and VI cauterizes on the point of the back, and I grant on the croupe and I other delves, and II sus the II espaules;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and II sus the wrists and II sus the tendons of the foot, and I suspend each joint of the hands and feet, and II suspend the fissures of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and remove the bones that are underneath the heel, which you do not burn.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never made a fire cautery on the bone, and the other on the stomach, and the other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And be careful, the more you make a fire cautery, the more help it provides, and it profits you.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And be careful, the patient does not feel pain in the fire cautery if it is done correctly, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be both large and small according to the parts and joints of the body, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the dough with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it is safe.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When the wound is healed in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healthy, then I make a fire cautery on the member according to its size and thinness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauterization be a small amount entered into the flesh.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of wounds as soon as it is safe.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And no time is it made to cauterize and at the hand and on the thigh and on the back, after the issue of the bone that makes the member motionless, and if it is not removed from the flesh.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and nothing else enters if it is not known of the members and the issues of the moving bones in the body.
de albaras	of scars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is aroused, and the art of medicine finds nothing, therefore cauterize with a small amount of caustic on the flesh, according to the quantity of the flesh, as long as the member is motionless and has its color.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then the treatment of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and of colic and wind, of each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mix all together, and bind with a cloth, and apply to the shoulder as often as it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by burning
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When syphilis appears at the beginning, and you see it stop, if the burning is done with a fire cautery that seems to form a circle, it should go around the entire syphilis.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And everyone says that you make a fire cautery at the gum of syphilis.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And everyone says that this does not seem right, because I doubt that it is ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to do this once.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the most correct thing is that they are burned outwards, at the cautery called "circular", as we have said in our mouth about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The first sentence to translate is "de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer". The translation of this line into English is
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When some have a disease called "adubelati", and it delays to die either by the excess it does or by the old age of the patient who is too weak (that is, too many) and has little blood, or by the tension.
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it hurting to die.
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	However, the cautery is done by pricking with thorns.
aprés le laisse ensi.	after it is left alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will struggle to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it perishing at all the cauterization, if you heat the cauterization of this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the environment of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has perceived the heat, and such are the cauterizations that the patient feels deflated in a certain way that the course of the pulse is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, if it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cauterization by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing more than a swelling of the limbs, as it also dries out the hands like the feet.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in the joint that can suffer from fire cautery, then sharpen the thorns to prick small and large, according to what is suitable for the joint or the disease.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cauterization of all parts as much as you remove all corruption, nothing remains of it, that all that is corrupted will not ossify.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then let it rest for three days, and apply oil to the burned parts as long as the blisters from the hot fire are still intact and all corruption has subsided.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the care of the burns caused by fire.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy children are born, that's good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then resume the cauterization where there is need for more corrupt legs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this malady has never been cured by medical treatment in the place of the fire cauterization.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but all cauterization with fire is greater help, and I have already said the cure of the ague disease in the division.
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take the amount you have at your disposal.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the porings that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it has happened that the feet were affected by a disease called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing to be done which hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	1. And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	2. It is to know that cauterization by fire and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	If you are scalding, then the scald is like a pen made of hot iron, and it should be made as large as possible so that all parts can be covered, and there should be subtle margins.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After you put the scald on all parts of the joint, turn your hand completely around the joint until it reaches the end of the joint.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	And it will remain for three days until it begins to excrete sweat.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a poultice of boiled wheat and leave it on all night, and the joint will become painful and will be desrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat the wound with ointment by applying it as soon as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	If they are converted through deflection of the heart, and many times it happens in hands and feet, then you must have a hot iron cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this way:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a nail or iron bar, or a feather quill, and put it on the joint and the tendon, which is to know how to remove corns.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the nail on so that it burns all around, then put a bit of hot wax, and hold your hand well, and press your hand as you turn until the margin of the nail reaches the root of the screw, and then find the hot iron way perfectly fitting near the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	The patient suffers from the pain of a bee sting for a little while.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then it will leave him alone, and it will die at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	1. I make another after that, as long as you are aware of all these that are in the course, then you cure the wounds that engorge blood.
li cure dou trembler	2. And you cure those that tremble.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble from cold, or fever, or another, if it comes that you must apply four cauteries or four on the back of the spine, one cauterization between each spine.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	And you apply an iron cauterization or a pearl cauterization, and at the stomach with the olive cauterization.
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If you let it tremble, and it will recover its health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	4. Of pustules that have burst.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	None of the time appear by defuers the corps baths, or pustules come from large materials corrupted.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	If it is necessary at the first when they appear that a fire cautery is made on each pustule's head:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery of mithra's coal, or if the point is seized by fire, or of the cautery of Aristotle's root, or at the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never is the cautery made at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and it cannot grow new wounds forward, but it is disordered by the superfluity that comes, and they are healthy.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is tied off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there have been great dislocations of blood from the artery that is covered by the wound that comes to the pardefuers, or at the incision of the abscess, or in the fire cautery of the member, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a great grief to cleanse.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And all that when there is none, if you have to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press as much as it can until the pain is calmed by your index finger, and no more blood comes out.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then put olive oil cauterys of various sizes that are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then I proceed, according to the size of the wound and the strength of the limb, and I route the cautery along the artery, and place the cautery on this vein or where you hold your thumb, and hold the cautery until it is no longer painful.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it hurts when you tie the vein with your other hand after the cautery, and the cautery is extinguished, then take immediately another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And continue to do this one after another until it is not painful.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and make sure you do not burn the nerve that is exposed, and no other harm comes to the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and be sure that when you do not cut the artery, it is not possible to cause pain immediately if the artery is large, as this can only be done by one of the four methods we have mentioned.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	If by cauterization or extraction it is not treated immediately, or by tightening the thread, or by medicines placed on it that cause pain, then
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	then it should be tied and extracted.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will perform the restoration of the tie very tightly with threads or to put things burning on, or other similar things, will not benefit from it if not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to no one and there is no medicine present, then you should place your index finger on the wound as we have said, and firmly press until it is painful in the wound and the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move the patient, but the cold water is often too cold that it makes the wound cold and swells and causes pain.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make up questions before those that have to do with what he knows about cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here comes the first sentence to translate: "ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	Our first chapter of medical treatises mentioned that for all diseases, if it is necessary to burn or use hot medicines, we must know the causes, effects, forms, and types of cauteries.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have written this chapter of cauteries for the head and neck, and I will enter this chapter through my own path because it is lighter to write about this than about other parts.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	2. And if I begin this, it is necessary, my dear, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	When there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you are foolishly doing this.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many methods of people come in the treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	If there are those who have become ill with such a disease that they died lightly by the force of the remedy they took for their disease and the greatness of their malice.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And this is cause for fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And those who say to you, 
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am hungry.
et li maladie est despitouse.	And the disease is untreatable.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is only by your consent that those who come to you who have this manner can be treated, but put more trust in your honor than in your covenant, and do not give in completely but wisely of what you are certain, and what you could have taken and lost.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prophecy and indication in the care of your patients, so that health may be converted.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this good reputation, fame, and memory will help you.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear friends, our Lords give you good understanding and right judgment, and if you will seek the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or if you have ordered this chapter by consulting physicians, according to what is done by physicians who practice cauterization, which I have advised for the chief joints, because you will find it more easily that which you will use.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief joint full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Sages, this disease often affects infants in the womb, and when the head is pulled too hard on the child's chin.
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and never has it been caused by anything that could not be found out.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease in adults, and in all those I have seen, it has always led to death.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And because it seems to me that I should make a chapter in part of the treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I see the child of whom the head was swollen with fever, and the chief grew larger each day until he could no longer bear it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and thought so much the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled between the bone of the shoulder and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the ointment is such that the moisture is between the shoulder and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you should give the patient a wide slice of the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and so long as the swelling corrects itself.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And here is the form of the spatulum:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	2. If the fever is more severe and the abscess is larger, then I will make cross-shaped cuts according to this form.
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	When the moisture is drying out the bone, and you see the signs of the corners of the cheek being pulled tight by each part, and the sudden jump is what you feel when you press your hand on the bone, and it is not a lie to say so.
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If you want to sell the cheek III wares according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	Then after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After pulling out the wrinkles and powders, and mix in wine and oil, and let it sit for five days.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then take the dressing and apply it to the wound with needles and pins, and let the cheek be evenly pressed, and then mix in dry, moisture-free meat with the surgeon as much as possible until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is to look or open the large end of the abscess, and assemble the angle.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for no time has it been in front.
aucune fois derrier;	never behind.
aucune fois en destre;	never to the right.
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Measure accordingly the size of the abscess opening and the angle of the wedge, and they are made according to what you have at your disposal.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and make sure you do not cover the artery.
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and come quickly to relieve pain, if the patient dies from dehydration and evacuation of blood.
de reume	of relume.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is any disease called "catarrh" in the ear or nostril, and the disease is ancient, and the cure by medicine does not help much, therefore it should be treated with cauterization if it covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is therefore necessary, can you see the eyes closed, that the patient makes a fist.
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	After rubbing the thigh with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then pull the patient's hand up along the entire cloth.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look at whether the vein bends, and the two are responded to after the ears, and they are not the same.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the veins with a sharp needle, then cut one and the other with a needle of II parts, as far as the size comes to the bone, and that is by the widest part of the fist.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, cut the cloth away from the artery and press on it with the needle, while cutting as much as possible, like II does to the bone.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is punctured, if the blood does not stop continuing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open with feeling, then it is necessary to measure the amount of spice for three doses, and then add and make it juicy to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and if it is necessary to give six doses of blood, and by chance more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is still attached to the bone, and the bandage that was applied does not come off, then tighten the wound and hold it in place, and the cure of antiseptic as long as it remains healthy.
de emigrainne	Of the migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the migraine comes, and the forehead is pounding, with pain in the temples and headache, and sometimes other symptoms, it is treated with medicinal cures and all remedies do not help, if we cut the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have experienced.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them if the patient makes the hair on his temples fall, and understands the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is quickly responded to rather than in any men who are too faint.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is responded to, then tightly grabs the neck of the patient from different directions, then rubs the face with a rough cloth, and wets the face with hot water until the artery opens clearly.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatula of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then lightly scorch the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up with pincers, and take off as many threads as there are from each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	When the artery is subtle, if it reaches the tip of the nose, then the loop of that part follows according to the number of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then it will not jump out without pain at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw out five pints of blood, about three.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, then draw out the blood in two pints of a double strong silk thread, so that no poison comes before the wound, and it comes out with the blood.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then tie off the excess that is between the two lines in that hour, and then, if you see, if it cauterizes as much as the bone, until the heads are tied.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And it is the patient's turn, if the helper does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the fire cautery helps to end the moisture.
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Because it is of greater help than moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the limb with many layers of soft cotton and ties it well made.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when one loosens it, if one uses dry medicines that make the wound clean and tight, and tents as long as it is safe.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if there is no artery cort without your work, if you hurry too much through the cauterization, or you use your hand with vitrol and tighten it until it is stained.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	If you do not have this present, then put your hand on the leg as much as it can be, and make it cold with water as much as possible, and hold it tightly as it can be.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	What is more dangerous and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire cautery, but the cuts should be well spaced to last longer on the wound.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the stomach is too empty, it retains less food.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it should have between the two cuts a large amount of spices, and then when you see the two legs filling up, hold the fire in your hand as long as it stays on the bone, and cover the vein with the two legs.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And let them be far apart between the two heads, for it is not easy to do this cauterization all at once.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the hairs are descending into veins that are soon to become dry and hot from fire, and there is no benefit from medicine, and you see the patient's face swelling up, and it feels like the limb is moving, and it seems like a convulsion;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	And the wounds are thin and moist, so that the hair of the paper is cut, and the papers are torn, and burned by the heat of the tears, if it is necessary for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And it was called the ancient "bruised cure," and that you should cut the patient's hair according to the disease, either at the front or the back, then I made three cuts or the back equally according to the length of the back.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and it should be one of the cuts like the other two, which I made at the front by advancing the scissors, and the others I made with the paper as a guide, and keep away from the incision of the arteries that are made with the paper.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and move your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound should have three to the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and make a piece of sponge and moisten with cloths the sore, then cut the sponge into pieces of two parts each, and this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that is made in the temple just before the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scar all the tissue that is between the two furrows throughout the entire facial skin that is under the bone, then make another piece of sponge just after the other second incision, and then remove this sponge.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	2. If the bone is broken in the first fence with the instrument called "cultellary," and it is very sharp on one side and very blunt on the other, do not be too sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	3. And cut the costelet along the bone to the knee, and the costelet is blunt towards the bone, and the bone as far as it reaches the second fence.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the veins that descend from the head as soon as the incision is continued until it opens the curtain, and then make another piece of sponge just after the other second furrow, and then remove this sponge.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	Then the pain is alleviated, and the patient expresses the limb for the pain taken.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then, in each fold, a piece of soft cloth is placed, and dampened sheets of linen and oil and vinegar are placed on top, and it is ensured that the patient does not get cold.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And at the third day, the linen is removed, and a large amount of watery mustard is applied, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other ointments that are used to treat wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	The first line of the text translates to "He takes away the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	If any blood clots come, you will see the hairs thin and brittle, the eyes waver, and the papers burn.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	When the hair grows, and if it causes pain, and the patient suffers;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	and you advise them of these accidents that these matters and this catharsis do not come from many veins, and the remedy which is in it if it is;
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to shave his head, then make a deep cut along the front of his head, and another wide one in the middle.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the fending of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be close to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move with the mingeir;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	And when the bone is exposed, if all the blood comes out onto an sponge, and then press between the two lips of the fending and put a piece of cotton on it, and tie it with lin;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then apply some softened wax mixed with oil, and keep it away from the fire.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is cold, if you rub the bone until it becomes rough and begins to crack, then the treatment of things that cause inflammation, which are like nails, is necessary.
En teil maniere:	In this way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of collogene, and make a paste.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And apply it to these wounds to cause inflammation for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the ear's chill
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that is done to the ears is one of the four things.
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Or grains, or beast, or mine piercing, or similar thing if it can be made like this.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	If you sow, like thistles, fires, and pits;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	If water flows, like hot and inflamed, and similar things;
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he pushes something into the ear hole or another way of thing that does not fit well in the ear, and it does not grow in the ear, if he puts the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the wound, if no drop of blue oil or oil of sinew is distilled, then the extraction is made;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and I make the patient hold their breath, and it stupefies the nostrils as they exhale, and put on the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and keep the ear at a distance;
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times comes out fire through this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come out, make the extraction with fine tweezers, and its form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If she jumps with force using her hands, it is good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If she does not, then she should perform an extraction from the subclavian gland with small difficulty.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if she does not jump by this, then I make a hole in the arm and cut off the end of the ear or the opening of the ear, and stop it which is inside the ear wax if it can enter with the hole.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the tail is formed because often comes so as we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if she does not come in this way, then he takes glue of the dog and takes the bones, and puts any instrument that is not for this purpose, and puts a piece of cotton inside.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the gluteal muscle through the incision or whatever it may be, and draw out further.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out of all these things that we have said, then do not hesitate to tear the ear off rather than cause an abscess and spasm.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of tearing if you do it first with the shoulder joint, and remove as much blood as possible according to its strength, then place the shoulder between your hands and turn the ear towards you, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or depending on it;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and so the burn is like a moon, as you approach the piercing, then the bone follows your pain, and the blood flows heavily in your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the cure until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grainy and begins to ooze, then apply the extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it cannot be squeezed, then apply the following treatment according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and give an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not make this mistake when you think the grain is moist from the ear's moisture, as long as you have made many pieces of it;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then use your fine tweezers and the sugar, as we have said, if the extractions are healing;
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the fever therefore that happens in the ear, it is necessary that the patient uses the condiement of the first essence and makes the ear ample with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them be placed on the same ear or where the wound is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps for that reason, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If it does not, then if you take many piers according to the length of your arm, and wash them in hot water, they will become lighter.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and then put the helper on one ear, and pull out from it its other parts, and carefully through another hole in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and continue to do this piercing over and over again until the pain subsides completely, and then it will be all better.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	If you see, if you take one joint and burn the other end of it as hot as possible until the pain increases, then it will be better.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then I made another incision as much as it needed, until it was all out, as we have said in the wound.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the removal of the fetus, if it is small in size, like a pea and similar things, cure as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large in size, it can be felt, by using forceps for the extraction.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and that is the thing that is easier to open in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the removal of the earwax from the ears, if you open it as we have said in the division and treat with distillations, but the cure does not work, if you look at the ear with the sun, it will work.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If he does not open it at all, if the needles are subtle, and if he does not notice, if he takes the rope of copper as it is formed:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be tight and wide and long.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And cut off the more subtle head of the ear according to the amount of suffering the patient has, then they will form the rope completely.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until you see it all.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey, then soak the rope of cotton as I have said in the hole.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not become sharp as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the decision of the verses, and you will find them or treat them with distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	If you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, then the form will be as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let silver or gold threads be inserted into the small holes, and then they should be distilled.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And to press the distillation with the well-made silver instrument, and if you see the raizer and envelope around the tip of the cotton,
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then your oil or juice will gush out, and whatever you see of your medicines in the canal, the canal should be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then pour the oil from the raizer all over the cotton, and press your hand together until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And it feels the pain of the patient, and it is the distillations that are given, and they are poured into the ear at any time, as they are distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And keep it from being too cold, as the medicine would not work if it were not bone-cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the ear's chill
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without having purulent otitis in both ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And this same thing happens as a result of swelling of the wound, or of the ear drum being torn, and these swellings never go away in the ear, if one cannot see.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And never has too much fluid been given, and it is seen that it is not good.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	The one that comes from the font is, if it cannot be seen, a sign of successful healing in other situations, and in this case, it is necessary to put the patient's ear to the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and observe:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the apparent inflammation, if it has healed completely, then this is the form of it:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And so, and turning and bending before and after, if it does not hurt the ear:
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the inflammation is around or at the edge of the ear, if you hold it with thin tweezers and a light grip, as long as it is not too tight:
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the exfoliation is in the ear, if I take a soft and light raser and scrape it slightly and heat it up a little, then I put it or cors of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the ointment that the patient hears is bitter, gently pierce, and keep your fingers away from the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent according to the large piercing of the ear, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do not use any ointment until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and apply pink ointment and powdered vitrol broiet.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see swelling in the ear, if it covers that you pull the tent and rub a smooth tent made of rose oil and wax, as long as the swelling is red.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure, as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	2. If the dislocation occurs, then dip a sponge and wring it out with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the dislocation which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the parchment's folds
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the cure that comes in paper from hairs when they are wet and dry, if you extend them with needles and tweezers, and the cope of a spatulum of its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then put the head vitriol broiet.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it is not decorted, then the fire cautery subtle lenticulaire is applied, and the cauterizer after the incision must be moistened.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And they are often repaired, but nothing dulls its roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the grit
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times, things come in papers from the hairs that seem crooked in their form and hardness, and for this it is this disease called "granular" and is an assembly of large moisture in the paper of these and soaking.
li ovraiges est telz:	The dissection is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	The granular is such that it is silent on one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make the wound larger, then lightly burn each part, then take it with forceps and the cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you do not burn it with feeling a little paper, if it does not hurt the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	When the dislocation is large, if it is assembled with a stitch, and the care is given as soon as it is healthy.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If it is small, if no force is applied, because the repairs will be slow and unnatural.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	If the dislocation descends towards the ear, if you turn it inside out, and the dislocation is held with tweezers, and the cuff presses from both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	If the paper is moved by the incision, it does not hurt anything.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	When the dislocation is cupped, if you lift the salty oil, and care for the leg as much as possible until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is woven into the sheets of papers used, and this happens more as children grow older, and it grieves their eyes, and they come to the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears are in their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because they lie down in their wet beds and sleep, and the papers of their cradles are soaked with the grease that envelops them and have the appearance of having been affected by the exinach that is open to the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand on your two and feel exinach in your eyes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the chapter is such that the surgeon places his head in your hand.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	Then take a piece of thread, and make a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach from each part, and then put it on.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two hands on both sides, so that the exirnach is assembled in the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then place the moisture in the spatumile and cut a fendure that is as wide as the wound you make in the healthy part of the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the thread as long as you can reach the exirnach.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in other arrangements, exirnach comes from the fendure, according to the shape of a piece of greasy wax.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	1. Pull the thread all around your two legs, and turn your left and right hand as much as it is possible until it is apart.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	2. And make sure you do not cut in the tendon, that you do not go to all the muscle until it is, and that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	3. And if the thread does not open at the beginning of the cut, then lightly open a little part of the cut until it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	4. Then pull the thread as we have said, then soften the threads with oil and water, and put it on the leg, and draw it well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	3. And if such men who bruise their sails and put on to corrupt the moisture which is dried up.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor when he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the leu, then the doctor should use incisions that are gentle when he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on paper that is not of its nature, and it is watched, if it harms the eyes, and brings forth methods of diseases as common tears and softening of papers and albugines, as long as it is due to the destruction of the hairs.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the cure is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cauterization, or by medicine according to what is in front of the cauterization or chapel, and it is made or by incision and stitching or by needles, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your left hand, then turn the paper of the oil to your right hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If she is converted, it is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, then insert an awl into all the holes.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	And make the edge of the paper or the hair grow from these hairs, and pull the thread through all the paper, and turn it to the other side.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then, in the other part of the paper, adjust the hair so that it is even with all the nails, from the large to the small.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then pull the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and drape on the paper, then sew a figure on the paper as you would with a needle, and if it is not equal to the quantity you see being lifted by the paper that is supposed to be drawn, then it will be correct.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if a part that has skill cuts much paper according to the quality of the paper, whether it is soft or not.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then do all the sentences you have signed in the second line, and start with large, sharp scars.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And it is one of the fissures near the natural hairs as they grow in size, then cut the root, then scrape the bone at one of the two corners, then scrape it all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then assemble the two lips at a stitch with a needle of one thread for all the fine hair, and remove the blood, and dry the excess hair on the nails at any glands you see, if you see this done.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	If this is not treated, then leave the stitching and threads for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound with dried things that are constricting, as the paper relaxes from the wound's moisture and assembly, but the stitching is too tight (as they say in old times), and it is uncomfortable.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you recognize the paper as a figure that is also like the force of fire, as we have told, at three incisions, follow the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes he who overcomes with equal strength according to the form as it is now:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not even, then take an awl or if it has one thread, and make the figure fit.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And cut another piece of thread as large as the largest needle, and then a smaller one, and sew them together evenly between your two threads.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then gently press your hand evenly, and gently press all the leather where you have made a cut, as we have experienced, then sew the two sides of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healthy.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And when the abscess comes to your incision, if the pain and swelling are alleviated by creams and compresses.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And never has it happened that the hair of the paper is converted.
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	If you follow what we have said about the incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	The sutures on both sides are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The patient is treated for bites if they follow this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And if you convert the paper and make it according to what I said, then make the bites by hand, and tie them as securely as the paper and the length of the staple is.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And cut as you hold the pieces, where you hold the threads.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble the two subtly, following what is underneath the paper oil, and draw the bites from the two parts formed.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And it leaves no wounds, and the leather that is stretched will become thin, hard, and wrinkled, as long as it is on it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, if the wound has strong forces, then the care until it is healthy.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is healed, and if the paper is lifted, and no more hair will be tied.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And it is the form of the second incision you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The veins are such that you need a fine needle, and I cut a thread of silk and thin.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then assemble the heads and soak the other slightly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then order in the chase the other thread of silk briefly, and note the chief of the thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's thread in your hand.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And if you can see the sun, then cut and decline the hair, for these are subtle and thin hairs, then pull out all the hair in one go at the root of the hair that is not yet gray, and trace it on the paper as you pull out the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the end of the chase, and pull out the hair in the chase, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then, pull your hand as soon as the hair grows to all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the hair is treated and the hair does not grow with it, then you will cut off the hair at the end of the thread as you have ordered, until the hair grows and you see it by the sight of the oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	However, if you cut off the hair and the thread, and close the oil and leave it for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the wound appears.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is short, then accompany the long hair of the cheeks with the one you left, until it is elongated and then lie down.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oily substance
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the food comes in the oil, if it comes in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	1. naturally, and 2. unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes through wounds, or cuts, or burns, and in similar ways.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of the wound is that you cut it, and clean the edges, and put on bandages of linen, and keep it until it is healthy.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And only that you use in the treatment of the wound things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, then the disease becomes worse than the first.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but it works on things that soften, like figs.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the head of the wound or gash and its seed is cooked, and the ointments are melted into no oil at all, and wrapped in a tent, and the treatment of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And your treasures are if you keep guard that it does not become wet according to the form it was before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and the cases we have said no one has been worse than the remedies of this disease, that it does not relapse according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the charge that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is truly called "acarati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and burn and cauterization and things similar.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the path of the dislocation is that if you prick with a needle, if it has double the thickness, and the thread in the char, and I feel the other side of the larmier as much as the first, so that the threads come in II chiés of the char.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then the char is at the end of all the needle, and the cap is wide in the saturate.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if it seems like on paper it returns according to what it should, that's good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, then take the razor and put it in the fender, and turn the paper, and make II fendures or cost the paper as much as it needs.
