de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat's gaping
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No time is there for medicine without the hands, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when that does not help, look at the patient's face in the sun, then press the patient's tongue to the instrument I have given you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the bone, if it has all been cut with a sharp knife, or if there are small thorns that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If it is not worth anything, then take a small hair, and pull it out of the patient's throat, then pull or cut off the hair with fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's throat is covered with sweat all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then fill me with cold water, and operate on the mouth, and the throat feels as if it is being swallowed, and it moves often with my hand.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the tongue feels the cold water, then it is.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not feel as we have said, if the patient smokes tobacco, with the instrument I mentioned in the uvea fumigation;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because it will feel ticklish.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fumigation if you press on it whether you can or if it has charcoal inside, and it is covered with a covering sheet in the environment, and in that place is the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then the fumigation drips on you, and the patient places the head of the chain in their mouth, closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes to the wound.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the wound hurts, and if it does not stop, then the fumigation is repeated many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And the patient suffers from thirst, and drinks salty and acidic things, and does not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And therefore it is necessary to follow this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the wound, if it can be seen, resembles stingray spines that can enter the mouth.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it seems like the beak of a surgeon, and it has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot hold.
et vez ci la forme:	and then its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The cauteries of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	The forms of similitudes of abscesses are, according to what the memory comes after each other in this book, and they are diverse in piercing and size.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is in two ways that one is itself in its similitude, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if by the bones or if they are in place.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the head of the tumor is different from that of the foundation, and the head of the tumor in the flesh is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if in abscesses we do not have to pierce much, as long as the bowel is dead according to its completion.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	If it happens that they believe they can perceive when they are not, and do not die according to their accomplishment, as if they were amputations of joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when the tumor comes from delightful joints, and it is left as long as it is raw, by chance if the ligament and nerve are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	If the amputation is of the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until the member is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	If it is of the foundation, then if you do not kill it immediately, it will be harmed.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is only necessary to perforate the amputation believed to be accomplished with digestion, as if the principal member were harmed, that it would not be cut off, and it would be long-lasting, and a fistula would be formed.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And cannot be cured in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you observe the opening of the aperture caused by the abscess, which is inflamed according to its completion, and it is when the pain is eased, and the fever subsides, and the alleviation of pain and burning, and the debate and agony of the inflammation of the abscess, and the other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary that you cut around the aperture of the abscess, and where it has opened.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And if the opening is long and thin, and the abscess is in the hands or fingers, or in the joints and arteries, and throughout these areas without any clotting.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those places, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the body, if it is necessary to leave the puncture until it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you do not love this beforehand, when the blood comes from him, and it is painful to defecate;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and make them more like him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if no abscess is found according to the size of the corse, according to what the member can endure.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you cut out the small abscesses, the large abscesses.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if in such abscesses or it is necessary to cut out the head, and close it.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When I have become as hard as cheese, and is dry, then it is necessary to make it like the bubbles.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	If it is of those that are cut at three angles, and if it is of those that are coped as the flint of fire, like the throats of the angers.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And if it is of those that one makes a round cut, and other sizes and appearances are coped.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, like superficial wounds that require you to cut it plainly.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the wound is large, and it has hooked great bowels, and you cut it, if you do not pull out all the bowels at once, but pull out a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then the wound stupifies and jumps to the other side, then you pull nothing else.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	1. Do this many times with great effort until the bow is entirely broken.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	2. If the patient's willpower is weak, whether due to women, young girls, or old age, they will not be able to endure great pain.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	2. If you have never seen the end of the bowel, and by chance the patient dies, you will not know it.

Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and if you have discovered your abscess, if the wound is small, look at how small the abscess wound is.

et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	5. And if there are large abscesses and they have ruptured, then tie each one with a thread so that one does not touch the other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have managed to remove a part of the hide, and it is well-groomed, then it is recommended that you fill the gap with expensive fabric or rough linen thread, and sew it tightly.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, the bone, and the treatment of scarring as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	When the dislocation occurs in your shoulder, if it is cold and wet, and there is much pain, and you should gently move the limb, and put it back in its place many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the patient persists in bleeding, and is under proper care and treatment, and the powders I mentioned in my hands are found in this book, and if it is not enough, then you should use warm compresses and dampened cloths with wine and olive oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in this way, and the patient's condition worsens, so that you must use drapes that are moistened with water and oil, or wine and oil vinegar, just as we have said, then...
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the suture and the wound, if necessary, as soon as it is healthy.

des soros	of blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the head comes to abscesses, and they are like us, as if it were a grapevine, and there are many similarities.

et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if there are those who are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt that the patient will not bleed, then it does not matter.

And the operations of the cutting if you are skilled with all the instruments called "enterostomy", whether the form comes after, what it contains.

Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	3. And the cutting of the dislocation is made on the severe part, if it is more flexible, because there is not much blood.

et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the incision to be similar to a sharp, rough, and bloody piercing, which could not be cut;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if we had not made any, we would have made a wound similar to a piercing.

des scrophules	The first sentence to translate is "des scrophules
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often, the abscess comes to the collarbone, and loosen the clamps, and the wounds, and never once do they come from another part or cut, and they are mutilated, and are misaligned with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And every scrofula is properly located on its side, as the wound and abscess of the chief are, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are numerous.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that which you see in good position at the wound, and is similar in color to the color of the heart, and is uniform in every part and is not like nerves of the arm or the conduit, and is not like a tumor;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if you can cover it with plasters, and scorch it in every part, and the lips of the knee as the knuckles, if you have mastery of it, as we have said in abscesses of the chief;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	1. And the patient should rest and rest, and be sure not to damage the nerve or vein, and not to stretch too much, as the hands may swell, and not look too early, as you may damage what you should not.

et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	3. and let it stay until the inflammation is pacified, and the wound is softened, and it begins to fall off.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	4. And if the uncircumcised part is swollen, then return to your own chapter as soon as you have completed it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then if you see a few small pimples on your index finger, such as nails and thumb.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if the pimple has a deep root, then you must only cut out that pimple with a strong double thread, but do not pull it; it will cause no harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then use the wound of fine cotton, then apply Egyptian ointment, and the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the entire wound, if you manage to gather the two lips of the wound, and hold them now, then there will be no excess as the wound is not too large.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and to treat it further, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those pimples that are superfluous, pierce them or let them heal;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce them like the one mentioned earlier, depending on the size, then apply ointments and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is being corrupted.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well healed, if the cure of cauterization is done correctly, then it will be healthy.
de squinance	The first line of the text translates to:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I have never seen such in our world, and it is their scripture according to their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the cut of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And it is not possible to help with this, because all the veins and the blood of the patient are at those who have the throat swollen in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the ears.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the hollow of the thigh, it is necessary to cover the epigastrium to avoid the destruction that comes from dislocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we wish to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it in three or four passes, with a small cut that traverses the two circles, or according to the quantity of the cut, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and they say that it is possible to cut the epigastrium when it has no cartilage, and the wounds are long enough;
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are poor, then it is necessary to extend the neck skin to the entire chin, then cut the ear as far as it reaches the chin;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the veins, if you see nothing, and then cut along the line of the facial muscle, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the swelling of the cheek that jumps out due to the fractured bone and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt of the dislocation, assemble the two lips of the wound as far as possible, and close it all so that you can feel the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medications that make the patient sleepy, until they are asleep.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not know how to do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the lack of blood is noticeable.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Because the shoulder is dislocated due to the patient's weakness, and they cannot move it, and they breathe through the wound, and it should be kept alive.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients advised leaving the wound open as long as the disease had not passed, and it had passed in three days or four. Therefore, they ordered to suture and treat the wound as soon as it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see a maiden who is being cut, and she has a piece of fabric in her throat, and part of her dress is torn.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I was called to cure him, and I found him already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and find the blood that came from it, and I am well that she had not much vein nor led only the gorge, and the blood came from this wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I rushed to his aid, found the wound, and cured it as soon as it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not reach the lady's side until she was angry of voice, and returned later to her disposition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I said that in the tailoring of the epigastric muscle there was no pain.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These hernias are called "thoracic hernia" and are large in color like a beefsteak, and are more common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and occur in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	The nature of this procedure is to reduce dislocation, which can occur due to accidents.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	However, a natural remedy does not exist for this procedure.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	The accident can occur in two ways: either it is similar to a large wound, or it is similar to an abscess that comes from the artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it is necessary to overcome it, and it can only be done with courage in the small incision, and one must search throughout the introducer.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you also have large hands and cannot do it, then the operation is like cutting our wounds, and if it is done, it must be done throughout its entire course, if there are no problems.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	1. And it pierces completely, and the cure is done as it should be, as long as it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	Of the head
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	1. There are many ways of us, of which I will tell all the appearances.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	1. And it is necessary that I die all the difference that is between whelp and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	1. I say that issue is calm and feverish, as long as the ebullitions have passed and is accomplished the porridge;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	1. But the fever and the calmness rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	1. With the newborn there is no calm or fever or pain, and it contains I sweat, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the dove's neck, and becomes thus like a wisp, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	They are classified into two types, either rough or smooth, or wet or dry, and of different colors as I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a newborn, that you first examine and search for the entangled one in all the instruments called "entangler", according to what its form brings or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	The manner of incising the abscess of the gums is to prick it more with a damp finger than with a dry one, and turn the two points frequently until you feel that the pus has ceased to flow, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the instrument and hold it steady as you force it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the abscess is moist, it is cut according to its color, just as we do with other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And afterwards, if there is no moisture, the head comes out fat, so make it into a cross, and take it with pliers, and gently scrape each part and warm the coat where you should lay it smoothly with the nail.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you do not scrape it smoothly, then lay it in pieces so that nothing comes out.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing comes out, it will return to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it demands a poc, and does not grieve you, then use the wound of some corrosive powders, and tighten the wound, and put calming remedies on the swelling, and cure other cures as long as it is healthy.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is large, if the two lips of the wound are clean, and the care of those who enjoin charge.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the vein is tense or other, and you haste, and use the leather of vitriol glove, and leave it for II or III days, until the wound pours pus, and rest the heat of the sore;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to the copper that is needed most.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See these forms of the entangled stones, and there are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	Large and moist and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are three kinds of stones that are called "alabar" and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Grant, moign, and petit, by encircling the fistules' apostilles.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are like the eyes of the eagles whose beaks are counted, and are of gold or silver or copper, and are more expensive than yellow ones, and are better at avoiding black holes for encircling the fistules' apostilles.
et sont de III manieres:	And they are in three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Great, medium, and small, according to the size of the abscesses.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the tumors are of many appearances, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Great, medium, and small.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	If there are birds with two holes of three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	And if the birds have three beaks, and they are of three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	And if the birds have two beaks, and birds with one beak, and they are of three kinds.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And this is necessary for their neck.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is made so sharp that it can cut through anything, even the skin, because it cannot touch the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And the introits of these are replaced with handgrips, so that the patient does not lose consciousness at the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	1. And there are three ways to it:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	2. grand, small, and misplaced, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	3. but only in the shoulder and arm, as with legs and arms, and hands, and fingers, and toes, and in similar parts;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	4. and no other instrument is ever used that resembles forceps, according to this form, but one is inserted in the wound;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he places it on no occasion in the shoulder that is strong and resistant to wounds and arteries, and it never returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	5. and no other men's hands ever swell when they are trying to correct the wound, as if they were female hands;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	6. and are swollen and inflamed, and those who see them cured think that it is according to this form of this line from .b. to .g.;
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scorch the fat, and employ the wound with medicinal burning char, then stitch the two lips of the wound together, and dress it as it is healing.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if it is crooked, and is made straight by its growth, as it is with women, if they are made in two pieces, by the resemblance of their limbs.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	If one is holding onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, then this line .b. to the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scorch the leather between the two lips, and remove the fat, and do what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, as long as it is healing.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	If the patient is not healthy, or if the incision is not fully healed, because the therapist does not rest, or due to the reabsorption of blood, it comes that you fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the dressing and grease have been removed, then treat it when it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	The first sentence to translate is "des apostemes des asselles". The translation of
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These apostles that come out of the hooves are ways for scrofulous hard nodules or callosities to form, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, which contain moisture, must be cut according to this form, along the line .b. and .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels within the abscess are out, if you employ a piece of clean linen, leave it there for another day, then take out all the linen and treat with ointment as needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scabs, then it is like we have said in the thorns, and if the wound is deep, then it should be cauterized as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sutured as it should be, if there are many hematomas and the vein becomes inflamed and infected.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the patient complains of pain when it is due to the artery, then it is cut; if there are hematomas, they should be removed.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel your pain, if you feel strain.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And if it is due to the vein, if we cut it loose.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is madness to cut this abscess, and at the same time when the screws and nails are removed and the skin is torn and out of place, and it is infected with other pustules.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one in charge must also avoid it, and in the one who has been pierced by arrows made of hair, which have been passed through the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then, apply the size of the nails, and remove the arrow from the feathers, as soon as it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle, and feel on the other side, and tighten the artery with a thread doubled into two, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of two arteries in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then do not insert the bone that is between the two fingers of an introducer as long as it does not cause pain, and if it does cause pain, release the abscess.

et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is of the size of the vein, then it is necessary to clean it with your hand the amount you have taken from the abscess all over the skin, then insert the needle into the bone you hold in your hand and feel, and if there is a thread doubled, then take it off the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the suture, as I have said, or one of the two ends of the thread to the corresponding bone.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the threads will not fray, if another needle is used throughout the entire thread from the first needle to the end of the suture at the incision, and the threads are tightened in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then tighten the suture as much as possible, then tighten the excess and leave what is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the linen cloth wet with wine and oil, then treat the wounds as needed until it is healthy;
des apostemes des ners	Of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	For abscesses of the nerves come in the artery and vein, they come when the nerves are too tight or due to too much work, and similar things happen.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with assistants and you must do it in all joints, and it is a great pain, and its color seems like the color of a corpse, and it is in more positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is tightened, it forms, if it feels great pain, and it is not in a state of being dead, but rather it is in a state of being alive;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it is very still in all parts, and it does not go before or after, nor does it come or go, and the one who is in joints cannot be made by force;
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance it may contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is at the head or front, makes the leather at the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the head is small, then it is held with nails, and the cradle at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then it spends in the hip, and burns it, then the bone and assembles the wound to the seam, and the cure as long as it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	large pus hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No time comes in the womb and does not affect another part of the body, and it is a disease called "funk" by its appearance, and it affects the root subtly, and the head is large.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And in some it is small and in others large.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I have seen one who had it in his belly and another whose belly was more similar to "funks" than anything else, and it had no difference, and they were white, had thin roots, and were trimmed, and decayed due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I found them and discovered in one there were 18 ounces, and in the other 6. The incisions should be made if you observe that the patient's skin is moist, and the color of the artel is bluish-green and moist with a subtle root.

et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and it is placed correctly, and if you do not hold it with your finger, then the wound will be held with your nails, and then the dressing.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they persist for three days, and the part is swollen and inflamed, if it is left until the swelling subsides, and gently scarifies the area.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If the copper is as you say, and you keep hold of the part of the thorn, it will not harm you.

cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the limb as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	2. Retain urination.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine if it is due to opulation of the urethra, or of the vein, or of the bowel, or of the stomach, or of similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not discharged, and you see that it is retained by the urethra which is at the junction or neck of the bladder, then it comes that the patient's pain is caused by the urethra being caught on its flesh.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And the penis is placed on the back, and the abdomen is extended from the part above the back, and the patient is restricted as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And therefore the bladder is constrained to express itself at the urethra as if the urine were discharged.

et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let silver be gently plucked out of thin hair, as if it were the quill of an owl.

et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess of the hair and cut off the end of the tail of the urethra, then anoint the urethra with oil or balsam and urine of onion and olive oil and German tarragon; and make the patient sit on the seat, and the patient's bladder and the verge moisten with oil and olive oil and German tarragon.

des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are scorchings or pains in the bladder, or if there is vomiting, and you see water and medicines being distilled, then do this to all the instrument called "caustic," and it is shaped like this:

de hernie carnouse	of hernia surgery
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Dew is nothing but an assembly of water or white soap, which is dissolved by the urine, which contains the semen.

dou chastrement	1. The text does not provide a sentence to
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	1. Injuries that are caused by violence are classified in our law, and this is why I do not want to discuss them in detail in this book.
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	2. It is necessary for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	3. The other reason is that the injuries are classified according to the response of the patient when asked about them and their treatment.
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	4. And the other reason is that we often have to perform surgery on animals for their benefit, such as on sheep and lambs, and goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	5. Therefore, injuries are classified in these two ways.
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	Either by attraction, or by burning.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one we make by attraction, let our hands be in hot water, as long as they are softened and while.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then pull on your hand, as long as it is back in place and you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the austerity of size:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	It is necessary that you pull the best, and press the leather of the joints to your left hand, then release the suspender, and cut each knot at each hip, when you have well burned them.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no sore or subtle sore that is near the veins.
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	And this manner of cauterization is more effective than that which is made by attraction, because attraction wears out with chance, no matter the size of the bones, and the beast desires luxury.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then cure the wound as long as it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	The translation of "des hermofrodites" is:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Heroism is according to two ways for men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	One is that between the two bones it is open as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and never once in cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is for women, and it has as much hair as a vine and the members.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the care of the mouth and stomach is that you cut all the loose charms and cure them as other wounds.
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, men whose urine leaps through the skin of their thighs, if there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of temptation.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tenting is a char that is placed on the natural part, as it is too ugly to see.
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and no women have had such a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you bind the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or fingers, and lightly cover it.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not let it get too far, because the blood does not come, then the cure of another cure until it is healthy.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	For another char that is not in the mouth of the mare, and the employs, and by chance it jumps forward, and appears as the appearance of a cow, and therefore they called the old "cow's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you are able to copy it, if as we have said, and cure it as soon as it is healthy.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	However, if the nature of the woman is not well understood, or the cough is small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that came from it.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by a strange char, or a subtle facial or espadrilles, and is made in front of the mare, or the cost, or the shoe, or whatever.
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and the design, and the birth, and by chance the flowers to have.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this if it is by the restraint of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the head is pressing against something, whether it's your body or another object.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is hard to remove, and it is close as it is, if you hurry, and it will turn back.
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	put your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs.
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then the two levers are formed, as long as the subtle fac is removed and over the tight ones.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take linen and oil, and put it on the limb, and make the woman lie down every hour, if it does not stick.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the pain is hard and sudden, then you must gently hold the joint as if it were a slate of marble.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the joints are cold, if the bone is spent and the flesh.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and use the remedies that quench blood, such as mercury, dragon's blood, incense, and a large amount of urine.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then make a large cut, if the wound cannot be sewn.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and it should be long, and a tent of dry linen is made.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat other wounds as needed while they are still healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marriage there comes a dislocation, if it is necessary to cut according to this manner, then it should not be enchanted with pins.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the incision of the scarlet fever, which is in the marriage, it should not be touched with firmness.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Embroideries are open veins that without customary scarring, and when they become old, they become thick.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	In the division of appearances and signs, I will mention those that require care.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are formed in the marriage, do not appear by feeling, unless it is with a firm cure.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are in the mouth of the marriage can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary that you put the woman in a cool house, then remove the nails from the horseshoe, and cut off the roots of the horsehair, then powder the medicines restricting blood, as well as those for dragon's blood and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then cut the horsehair and put it in cold water for an hour, then dry it.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	And if the blood comes out, if you put it in a decoction of sumac and the juice of grenate pomes and gall and similar things, then take flour of oats, mix it with honey and vinegar, and apply it to his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If it is inflamed, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, make him lie down on his back and tie his arms tightly;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take the wine, and the juice of plums or willow with it, and make him drink.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when he has vomited, take care of the wound with an ointment as soon as it is healthy.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And the ointment called "albathir" is red and resembles the spicy herb "thula", if it is effective, then it is similar to the turmeric.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take care of him as soon as he is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the abscesses of the married woman
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come to the married woman, such as chancre and other purulent abscesses, herpes and fistulas and blisters and chancroids and abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is therefore necessary that I give in this treatment the first aid for the wound that comes in the marriage, which is not the worst of wounds but is caused by bows.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	And if you see the fire cautery, then look at whether the wound is still in the beginning of its arrival, and see for caution and fever, and if it becomes red, you will see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	However, do not force the pearl, but make it as long as the pain is eased.
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	And then make the patient sit on the bed, and have two pillows under his head, and support his back and assemble his limbs as to hold the leg.
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	And let his thighs be expanded, and put on his boots above his knees, and tie them well with a bow.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then proceed the dressing towards the left side of the chest, and insert the instrument used to open the mouth of the marriage, and after that comes the form.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And it is necessary that when you see the instrument being inserted, you fix the rait first to know the fitting of the marriage, so that what comes out of the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	And if the rait is larger, it is necessary to cover the fitting of the marriage with cloth, so that the rait does not hurt.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	It is necessary that he places the instrument's horn at the joint, and grinds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is open, and it is touched with wet hands, if it comes into contact with the head, at the spinal marrow.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the wound is visible, it comes that you put in the wound soft tentacles in olive oil or green vegetable oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	And put the tent of the wound at the edge of the marsh, and put through the marsh and through the clean soft tentacles in the water or in the mud that are cooked.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the cure after two days of ointment coming to this, as long as it is healthy.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	And no time the wound and the plague are raised by honey and vinegar, and then vinegar or roots of lilies and Aristotle are cooked.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then comes the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is dressed in the marsh, then it comes to your attention that you should not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	Most important is the dance where she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are such when you see the woman press against the wall, and desires to smell the aroma of amber.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	However, do not delay in giving birth to the children.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	Then you know that these children are according to the natural figure, and they are from your own chief, and the second one with him.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	When you see these signs, if it is necessary to lightly press on his abdomen, if the child is cold.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	If he descends from his throne, and if it is with him, and the marriage of his superfluities by good cleaning.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	And that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it never comes on its own piercings, and it comes from the chest or neck, and the hands, or it comes from the belly or stomach, and it is converted by chance with his collar, and by other harmful figures.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	If it is necessary for the dance that she be skilled and subtle in these things, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures of how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	When the child comes out of its head naturally, and the mother gives birth with great effort, and her virtues are weak, if it is placed on a pillow or the women hold it.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and its nature is olive oil or fenugreek, and then boil the baby between its two little feet, and this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and cut the second one, and cut as much as the moisture that is left behind.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and cut the woman's stomach as much as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clyster the woman with muslin of fenugreek with olive oil.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Then I will prepare and administer the anesthetic, and hold their mouth and nose for an hour.
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If you are now ready, I will insert the enema.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the hands do not come out quickly, it will be necessary to gently move them a little at a time.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	And if they do not go in, the woman should sit on the edge of the bed, and gently lift the feet up.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	Then the woman should lie down on the ground, and tie her feet together so she does not fall.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands do not go in, and the enema dies, she should hold her hands on the side that is closest to her, remove the child, and reset it gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot that was cut off
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the children come to their toes, if they can put it on high.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it a little at a time, until it is even.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then pull on the toes and stretch it a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump like a knot, if it is commanded to pull, and I make it tighter by condensing?
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps, may God see.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump high jumps, as we have said, if the shoe is tightened a little at a time until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the issue of the child with its gums
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, if she holds it with her hands a little at a time.

de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of the issue of the child who comes out wide with a hand during birth.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to bring the hand back.

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	2. In the same way for all the second part.

adonques si istra legierement.	If you handle it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	It is said that they are born many times, and never in the third or fourth month.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	And this is a strange thing, and few come to know it.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two things are strange, and they do not live long, and have little name.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are destroyed by the sickle which devisages them, which is bound to the hood.

et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And make it as it is worth to greet.
de plusors enfans	Of more children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	No times are formed in the marrying I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the great joy, and cover that the sick dance, because by chance similar things come to it;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	If you make it according to this that is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead or pregnant child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to open with hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	If it happens that you should cut yourself on the woman's body and there is no accident or she dies of pain.

des plaies	wounds
