dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre." In English,
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The dislocations of the abdomen are large and numerous and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound no time the intestine is leaped, or the intestines are injured by it, by the insertion of others.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stomach is more painful, and no time the small wound is better than the large, because one has to reinsert the intestines several times if one does not put them back in place each time.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	For the intestines swell so much that they feel the pain, if they return more often, and for the reason that it weakens the wound, for the reason that we sometimes have to reset the dislocation of the shoulder, for the reason that it causes great pain and injury.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you say that the intestinal rupture occurs in four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common types of abdominal hernia are the abdominal hernia and the hernia in other parts of the body, and the other two types of hernias are common in other parts of the body.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more common with the abdominal hernia, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no inflammation in the intestines, and it is a difficult matter to set, this is done by one of the following two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is swollen, treat it in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soften an sponge or a damp cloth only, or wash it with cold water and rinse it, and clean the intestines as much as they will absorb.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And no time has it been made to keep the wound closed and it is dead that it does not want to be opened.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the blooming depart, if the intestines are swollen or stretched and the veins are twisted, for this is the cause of the narrow entry of something.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound in the wound with the instrument of coping the blood;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is dead that it does not cut the size, that no one needs to cut in great need and has not.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the reason for the splitting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If the thread cuts through the feather and does not pass, and if it looks like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine springs forth, if you return it according to its natural form in its own place, if you can, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	If the wound is large and it is in the lower abdomen, then it is necessary that you lay the patient on their stomach, and raise their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	If the wound is in the lower abdomen, then it is necessary that you raise the head and the legs higher than the abdominal walls, and if the wounded part is one of the two, then you should agree that the raised part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And it is necessary to manage what I say about large and dirty wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	The first sentence translates to: "If it hurts slightly, then take your hand and apply wet bandages to all the wounds on your hand, and gather your lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	The second sentence translates to: "This is the common way to stitch wounds. You take an awl or several, according to the size of the wound's depth, then leave the end of the wound open and sew it with a needle thread strong.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	The third sentence translates to: "Then pierce the two ends of the leather with the two ends of the suture thread, which is loose from the leather, as long as you can pierce it from that side, and assemble the two ends of the suture thread with the four.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the strain of a double thread through the needle of II part, then assemble the II heads of the wound, and then leave I two spicules, and then choose another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then lay the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to what you are used to with needles, until all the wound is held in place.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be sharp and not too large, for sharp needles close the wound completely, and very large ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For it is necessary that they be sharp.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not thrust the nails too far into the horse's shoulder and leather, which do not hold and cause the wound to reopen in front of the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cover the heads of the nails to prevent them from causing inflammation in the patient's sleep, and use cloths or blankets on the heads of the nails to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with nails is more convenient in small wounds, because it does not cause an aguille or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it is that you sew the two ends of the leather with the two ends of the thread, and they are sewn together with one nail or it has a strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	When you have perceived these four conditions assembled, first reset the needle at the part where you began, in the manner we have described for the threads.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and insert a splice between each stitch of the large end of one thread.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch saves the man, and I saw a wound that some had in their bellies, which was caused by a needle, and it was more than one palm wide, and it had intestines that were more than two palms wide, and it was the wound in his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I took the intestine and after it had been out for 24 hours, it was 15 years old, and the wound was healed, and I cured it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And he saw the blood that would not stop, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not cure it with ointment, because I am in II the shoulder where they do not find any, and no medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put on more than twice the amount of cotton lint under the wound, and wash it with honey as often as it is healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or you may say the two ways of dressing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pull out the thread from the part that is most difficult to sew.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has perceived the right way in the right direction, if you have pulled the needle or cut it or made the thread perceive another part of the difficult part, and make it perceive from another part of the easy part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And when they understand this method, if you also follow the pliers like they do the hair, and once you shave one side, then you take the other, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galen himself uses, is if it is done correctly by anyone, which naturally brings together the two parts, and applies one end of the beard to the other, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert an awl or beard of iron close to the skin, and make a mark on that part only, and leave the two ends of the beard of hair.

puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then I make it feel at both parts of the wound that are most hurtful to you.

Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this word, and no one testifies, you must sew the belly to the needles, or there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And it must be sewn one needle at a time, and the other at another, in the way that these are sewn together.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And you ask if when the fracture is near the stomach, it is the cost more painful than others in the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	They judge the wound if it is like the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that if you clean the fresh wound with all its blood, but if it has not moved, then reset the intestine and the gut;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on the powder enjanning char, and if it has moved, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bowed;

et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, then use this: make a poultice of the bowel, cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no other medicine in other preparations, the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound is not a principle member, then use light oil of tamarind or rose oil, and apply it to the edges, and dry the stitches;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If he feels pain or dryness in the bowels, and it happens many times, if the clyster of black wine is given, and at the same time the dryness comes to the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the bowel is hard and sore, and it is lighter than the stomach when it is large.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The small intestine, which is called "young," cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the veins that surround it, as well as the subtlety of the entire body and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gush of blood comes from the wound, and it is set in place as the intestine, while it is fresh.

Then pull the joint that is between the bones, and hold the head of the arrow until it is fully pulled out of the wound, and then straighten the extraction point where the arrowhead bites.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	If the intestine is torn and the wound is small, then it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were wounded or in the belly of a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And the wound was at the left side of the stomach, and it became a fistula and contained the excrement and vomit.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop refining it until it was healthy, and I saw the result.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I see him suffering, I doubt that the patient has no harm in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he has no harm, but delays in better conditions, and eats and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and there is no one who says that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he should be treated in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	first examine large testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when he has stretched his mouth over the wound, if she puts it with her lips, so that she draws back her mouth.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then she covers the testis, and this remains if he cannot slip, then she causes another convulsion after in that way until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	And the wound is counted.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the intestine is caught in the abdomen, and there is no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a very fine thread that is sutured with the intestine of an animal, in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this intestinal thread that is free, and then tie it to the head of the other thread I lin thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and count the intestine, and reset it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of stitching is not worse than according to the course of love and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, then it is similar when it is in one of the intestinal grails, if it does not heal or become healthy, then it should be treated with caution.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	All wounds and abscesses, when they heal, are called 'fistulas' if they are completely closed, and likewise if they are small and rounded.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is according to the true node that needs to be hard and bluish, where there is no pain, and it is as fine as the tail of a pegasus.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And never in a clear leap bow, and at other times it is thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Never in a small amount, and at other times quite.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that all wounds that are not healed, and there is no pain, it is only due to one of the eight causes.
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This is to know, by the small pain of blood or grief.
ou por sa malice;	or because of malice.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because of the hard teeth, and the mouth, which does not leave it in peace.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or he has too much bowel.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the food is spoiled, and the matter is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because of the corruption, which is a plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in the region, which is slow to digest, and slow to health, and flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	If he has veins or not:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have shown you all these causes, signs, and remedies for medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	1. It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistulas, which is performed by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Wounds that occur in all parts of the corpse's body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For he has fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the face, intestines, bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if a part that comes from the proper member of the body is affected, and similar to it;
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this kind are of painful healing, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is no fistula that comes to the place where I have said it would, and you are a practitioner of the cure, and you see it occurring, then take a tent made of linen or iron, if you wish; if the fistula is straight.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is twisted, then search for a small tent made of linen or iron, because the threads will twist around the tortuosity.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula is closed by hands and you do not find it well by tents, then search for the fistula by the other hand, because the moisture is cut from one part to another, and it is cleaned.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then, if you are wise, you will know whether it is bone or flesh, and ask the patient to indicate where they feel pain when you press with your hand, and the limb where it is felt.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the limb and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or any of the limbs I have mentioned, if the couch follows what I have said, and the force and the crooked ones that are corrupt;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then, when the wound is healed, and the fistula is well-made in the right place, if you press with the couch, as far as you can, then take fine tentacules of medicine ague, and insert them at the end of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that has been accumulated in the fund.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then he puts antiseptic ointments on the healthy skin, as much as needed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healthy by this, then the cauterization is done as we have said, and if the part is corrupted by the fistula, then it is cut out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If it does not hurt the nerves or the principal limbs, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it is discovered that there is infection and blackening, and the patient remains as long as the infection is not completely healed, then the treatment of unhealthy skin ointments is done as much as needed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healthy, and the bowels are not relieved as before, you should know that you are not able to do this:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If the dislocation occurs and you are able to do so, and remove all the corruption, then restore the shoulder.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is in good health, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, you should know that the corruption is too deep, and you will not be able to remove it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other way but to cut it out.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	If it is small and corrupted, and you can remove it with tweezers, if the instrument is suitable for this purpose, and if there are more, then remove them all.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if the moisture is contrary to you, and there is no error, then cope with it and make it char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	If you do not cut the wound an hour ago, then put something to stop the bleeding, and leave it until the pus comes out of the bones, and then the bones will become lighter.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	If it is large bones, such as thigh or knee, if you only treat the infection until blackness appears throughout the area, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	If it is a large part of the bone that has become corrupted and comes out of the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it is necessary to cover and protect all the infected area and treat it as soon as possible.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of an example of a fissure that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can learn from it and help in your practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man who had a pain in his leg for many years, which was caused by the heart, so that the matter came to the leg, and he was swept away by a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but they overlapped so much that the abscess was opened, and it corrupted with matter, and became a fissure, and there came out pus that all the bowels were torn out and the heart was full of moisture.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And for the first two years, and they received no knowledge in the art of hands, as long as I was called, and I saw their leg and the medicines used to cure them, and what died from the pustules of great pain.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And it became red in the cheeks of youth, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of these holes, and then checked all the holes, and found that some came together at the other part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I thought furthermore, and in one of the pustules I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and decayed, and it came from the bone itself.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was he who appeared from the corrupted bone, and I made sure there was no other corruption, since that was what I was.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to restore the wound of soreness with long tents, and it could not be sewn.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	Then I returned and discovered the bone as before, and found continuous corruption in the bone, and it was decayed, and then I set the bone, and I thought about sewing the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not cut through the bone so far that it would reach all its parts, then I restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was healed and sutured tightly, and I did not want to return to the operation because of the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because the evacuation of blood is often, but it was completely healthy, and a hard stone was found in the bone, and it was well positioned and had no harm or contradiction at all, nor in the air nor coming out.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken at any joint of the arm, then it should be set in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take two pieces of wood, and pull on them, and command that it does not extend higher than the top of the bone.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And then put another piece of wood that is larger than the first one, and lie it across the bone, and hold the head, so that you can pull the broken end out of the bone, and cut the head off at the joint where you see it set, so that it does not break the head.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And then put a bandage or a table around the bone to cover the broken end of the bone.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	It is necessary to soak as much as possible and can be seen and felt the corruption, and soak again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the environment or a part of it, if the cart is taken out completely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the incision in place, and then it is of one part to another the corruption, and the soaking water is long from the corruption pit, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, if the corrupted joint is cut, and it is the bone or it contains another part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption spreads to the continuation of the second joints, if there is no other enemy than cold;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	If the corruption is in the fingertips or the toe, if it is painful there, but it must be that you investigate this corrosion as to how it opens;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and it is made in all ways that you can think of, but the vein or the nerve will not oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and you ask that the incision and the soles cover these bones which are many, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their bigness and their subtlety, and their growth and their diminution, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to adjust the appearance of each instrument of its kind.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And you claim that the work will show the instrument you will use, according to the knowledge of this art, and testifies the ways of the diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you are not sure about the instrument you will use according to what is necessary for this.
dou feu	The first line "dou feu
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads of the shoulders either fall due to denseness, or due to hardness.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have cured the corrosion caused by the medicine, and it does not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that member up to the league or where the corrosion comes, if the malady is caused by death or by malice, which is greater, of the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	When the signs appear that the limb becomes black, if it seems to be from burning heat, and then after turning black, it spreads to all parts of the member, causing corrosion.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you feel intense pain, and it is due to the impact of certain beasts' venoms, like that of a sea scorpion and wasp, and the corrosion is at the tip of the member, and it does not come out easily with your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes out easily with your hand, if the puncture is at the joint, if the corrosion does not come out easily from the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	If it comes to the arm, if the shoulder hurts.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	If it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no way to save it except for the amount of its courage.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And so, when the corrosion comes or pain.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes in the first joint, if the shoulder is after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	If it comes with pain, if the shoulder has all the courage.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	If it goes up the leg, if the shoulder is at the joint of the thigh.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	If it comes from the thigh, if there is no other way but to kill the patient.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	1. And the way to cope with or soothe the member is if you tie it off and cut away some of the members on one side, and others on the other side, and then stretch out the cord that is between the two members at a wide spacing, as long as the bone is discovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	2. Then the relief or soothe, and use of cloth, if it does not touch the healthy skin, and go to the surgeon for another wound and gangrene.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	3. And if the evacuation of blood comes when you work, if you cauterize the skin hastily, or if you put on any restraining powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as soon as it is completed, then tie the affected limb with a flexible bandage, and treat it as soon as it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened in my home in short:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	it happened to me a blackness that seemed to be burning, and this corrosion came first in my little child's poop, so it consumed the whole of it.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when I saw the corrosion, if it could cover the child's poop, and it was healthy:
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and later when I returned with the corrosion or feces from the hand, and it came to me, and I did some things reflective after the purification of the corrosion, and it could not stop the corrosions:
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	I will try to pass my hand over it, and I do not expect any effect from the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I doubted that if I cut my hand, it would not bleed because the strength of his arm was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	He then desperately returned to his land and managed to close his hand, and he was saved.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I did not have this story to tell because it is another matter, and it is their craft.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No one has ever had an aposteme in the wild boar, and it takes as long as it makes a great assembly of arrows.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they are torn apart and pierced, and with a jump the bowels are emptied, and the patient is relieved of his pain, just as some slaves.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that is covered is as soft as I plucked off hairs, and does not reach the bone or nerve, and such disease if called "healthy", but is actually called "fissure".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it reaches the bone, then it is called "fissure".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the skin if it is that you cut through completely, and at the same time when it is as soft as I plucked off hairs, just like some hairs.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not let it remain for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are engaged and the hair is growing, and the corruption is not yet complete, and the hair is long, then the cure is to curl it:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look at if the breasts are large, and the smell of the wound is unpleasant, therefore curl the breast with Egyptian medicine that has been made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take ashes, oil, and turpentine, and mix them together, then place the mixture in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and as thick as honey:
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	Then take this according to your need, and make it in the form of an ointment and honey, and cleanse the face, and draw out the pustule.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine on for two hours, then draw it out by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this as many times as the breast is swollen and the pus has stopped.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And never use an ointment of smoke until this medicine is present, and if you have ash from grape vine, and pour hot water over it, then let it drip, and when you see that the breast is well-swollen, cleanse it with the ointment.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear it, and the Egyptian medicine does not quell it with fire, then the poultice of fire and honey should be applied, or there should be a little bleeding.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you poultice with honey and wine, which has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the wound aerated.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you are sure that the breast is well purified, if the poultice made with what is most suitable for the wound is applied, and it is not too hot, and they make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	If you choose to cauterize with some medicines and ointments, which I have mentioned the properties or treatment of the ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the wound is small, and the cautery does not enter, then enlarge the opening with a iron pin, and put in a tent of the Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, as much as it is smeared;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, then the cost and it leaves only the head or the cautery can enter, and if the wound that oozes blood is above, then the cup or more below the head than it is;
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is empty, if it is not left alone to rest.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you do not hold your breath in such a way that the belly does not rise to the lowest part of the body where it is, because when the belly is empty, if it is not left alone to rest and you do not hold your breath in such a way that it appears in half the way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the belly rises lightly and does not leave any of the belly:
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to make it better for the patient and they are put on the limb that covers all of the patient:

et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then remove the dressing in the morning or at another time, and when you examine the wound, if you find a different layer, replace the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become wet and indigestible after the first year, it is known that the breasts will not lactate.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the venomous serpents are located far from the long tenses, do not despair about your health, as your health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For it has many methods of making incisions in its wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if it is not digested, after a day, you may see that the nipples are hard.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the nipples are not digested, and they become hard, if you use wet medicines in substance and dry ones in virtue, as an ointment is defined, because it has a great part of sulfur, and this is the rear medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	1. Take defattening ointment, and apply it with rose oil, and the ash of white wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	2. Then preserve and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	3. And then apply the dressing, and it is kept in the breast, and never once does an aristocrat administer it, and roots of the blue lily, which is also like flour and cinnamon;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	1. For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	1. Cut the, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	2. If the wound is long, and not cured by this cure, then you should know that the corruption has become established, and it makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard members, or in the joints.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	3. If the cure of the fistula cure is as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	4. Paralysis is an abscess that often occurs due to the swelling of the thumb or little finger of the hand, or by chance in other fingers.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	5. And when it is inflamed, and not taken care of, if it comes to an abscess, and runs and gets worse until it reaches the root of the thumb, or by chance it reaches all the way.

li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I made the joint healthy, and no accidents happened when I moved it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And there was an arrow in the neck of a horse, and it was the Arabian arrow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew the barbs, and very subtle when I translated it, and the horse was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And there was a wound on the man, which he thought was in his stomach or chest, and he thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then it had been XXX days, and if it had not been in its place.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I opened the wound, I dressed it, and it healed, and there was no accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a man had a wound on his chest or back, and it was infected.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the wound did not heal, and it did not adjust its natural positions, and it was not found in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if another man had a wound on his face, and it was infected.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	The patient will suffer greatly before the dislocation is treated.
et mout d’autres semblans.	Other similar cases may occur.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was an arrowhead in the thigh of the king's son, who had it for a long time and it was slightly inclined to the left side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	The arrowhead was completely removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for the treatment after it had been stuck for three years.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very tightly closed.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried everything subtly to find it, but I did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a sharp and painful sensation in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead I had put in his throat, because he did not gag.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I saw it was from an arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I placed the plaster on my hands, and dressed the wound on the right side, and it took a long time for the patient to feel the arrowhead enter his flesh.
et il le me dist.	And he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied the poultice of the corrosive medicine on my hands, and it was covered with a layer of plaster, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow that was stuck in the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I dressed the wound with the poultice of the corrosive medicine on the overturned plaster, and as the head of the arrow became visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it takes well to the end in four months, and then the wound is healed if I have anchored the nails with my hands on both sides, and it cannot be undone.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I will continue to refine and engineer ways of extraction, as long as I have the nails well made, according to how the form will be in the end of this chapter, as I heal and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Therefore, I will restore it, and the wound was soothed, and the patient's health was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I said the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your cure to what I will say, because the books cannot fully describe it;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the skilled masters make good use of many small things, and of what is present and lacking, nine operations, and a variety of instruments, in the descent of things that are drawn in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows do not come from the limbs or they are not cut off in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the arm or they enter, or by another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is cut off by the arm or it enters, is an arrow that has been inserted into the flesh, and it will never be cut off again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	If she does not leap now, if she leaves it as it is, and it becomes entangled in the hair, and the result is the injury.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if she becomes stuck in the bone, and she cannot move, if she leaves it alone for no reason, and moves each joint;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps, and if she does not jump now, if it is not cut deeply enough, as long as the bone is sharp, and then it will be difficult to remove;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and it will be near one of the bellies of the shoulder, and some of the accidents I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If it is not burned, but left as it is until it grows even after some days, it is because the shaft comes out and that causes death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the dislocation is not due to the bone alone, and does not cause pain, and there have been no previous accidents, then it is not a serious matter.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it becomes very thick and cannot be inserted further, if you administer tarters otherwise, as I have said to you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the head as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is reset in the shoulder, and one cannot see it, if they want to try everything.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, if there is no suitable instrument available.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you do not press for the wound's relief and for the shaft's removal, if it does not hurt as much as the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	When you pull the arrow out, and if it has ears (earplugs) that hold on, then break or crush the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Even if you don't break the arrow, pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not manage to do it once, if the patient is still resistant until the end, then pull out, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If the dislocation occurs against the joint, and you ignore what we have said about the cure in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And you are wounded by the incision of the nerve and vein, and put your hand on it when you pull out the arrow more firmly, whether slowly or quickly, or firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And place the patient according to the form it was in when the arrow struck, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that came from another part, or it opened no thing of his, or the skin is shrunk in some place if you see or feel it:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then measure according to size, as long as the thorns can take hold, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it does not come now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you turn your round hand around as it enters the bone, until it expands the bone, then it will exit.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and then resume the extraction as soon as it comes:
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is from the arrowhead and is stuck, it is cut at all strokes.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is stuck, and you see the instrument being administered, if it is an instrument with sharp points, then the arrowhead enters the instrument's hair;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then cut further, and if the arrowhead is hair, if it cuts the instrument at the tip entering, to lighten the extraction;
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	When the arrowhead is inserted, if it reaches the entire cavity or the venomous substance, then you must first treat the wound as best as possible.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the belly, or in the stomach, or in the chest, and it is protruding, then you cover it with a cloth, it holds;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep the vein and the nerve, then extract, then clean the wound, it is easier.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment as soon as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the arrows' barbs that are used to extract arrows resembles a beak of an owl, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are several ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the abscess.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The pointed end of the hair is similar to the beak of a sparrow, to be inserted at the tip of the arrowhead, in the same way as this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tails to insert and to pick is similar to this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	veins that are healthy are XXXI, but if there is a headache of XVI, it means:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two bats that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbs".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two wounds that are in the two hairs, which are called "aspirations
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the wound that is in the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the wound that is at the top of the head.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two gouges that are out of col.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the wounds that are in the lips of those that are out of the mouth, and these are the wounds that are called "augeherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two wounds that are cut into the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The wounds that are usually found in one arm are five.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the temporal wound, which is on the left side of the chest, and it is called the "temporal wound" by the people.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The head of the shoulder is called "fast" and is composed of thecephalic and basilar parts, and they call it the "bone of the shoulder".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And if the basilar part is on the west side, and they call it the "shoulder bone", and it is under the fornix, and it is the one that is easily accessible, which is open clearly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the savette is the vein that is between the auricular and anal, and if it rains.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg, and at the ankle, there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is the corbier of the right ankle, and the second one is the suture at the left ankle.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	The vein that is called "nestle" is located in the ankle of the other leg.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	In the other leg, there are three veins different from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sinus of the veins that are after the ears can be helped by old catheters and drains.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the quality of the sinus is, as I say, and it is that you remove the head of the patient, and wipe the foot or the veins are of a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then the patient's throat becomes red, as long as the veins are visible behind the ears and the two dependent on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	1. If you feel pain in your shoulder, and if you sense weakness in your arm, then seek help.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	2. Then take the scalpel, and cut through the vein as close to the bone as possible, then gently hold the vein with your entire hand until it bleeds well, and then make sure the blood flows freely until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	3. Then stretch and hold it, as long as it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	4. And I have already said the incision and fire cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	5. The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if they are old and hard, and if they have been blocked, and if they have been narrowed, and if the tears flow from them;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and you can judge its quality as being quite healthy if I say so:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient pulls on his chest, until the veins open widely.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels the pain in his ribs, and then signs of enchantment.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently feel the pulse at the top of your ribs, and cut the thread below, and gently pull up the vein and the skin, as you have done in the other veins, and make sure to remove enough blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then relax the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then the ligature is formed and left as long as it remains healthy.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their strength and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the health of the cranial bone, and it is affected by ancient diseases of the face, migration, and wounds.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And if the patient is in pain when the surgeon strains his neck while drawing the vein, as long as the vein is exposed.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "forceps," whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and hold it firmly with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the cloth at the neck, and hold the vein until it is safe and never once with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Indeed, only the fire should be too large.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the safe way is to cross it, because the ointment is near, and by chance the fire may be too hot when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The safe way for the two veins that are in the two arms is to help the patient with the pain, and the bend, and the wound, and the urine in the oil, and many diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and assess the quality of their health if it is that the patient strains his neck by twisting any joint, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and if the patient has a long, narrow neck, because there is no cartilage.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the neck is slender, by chance if it is broken.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make a deep incision, as much as you can, and then cut the skin, and it heals well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The vein of the healthy one is not weak if it is long and slender, and it does not cause pain or disease in the face, as does inflammation and rash that comes with age.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the wound is considered to be good if the patient complains of pain in his chest, then tighten his neck in your left hand, and take a thin tweezer, and scratch off the eyelid in the eye socket that is between the two eyes, because the wound does not open well, and it will now start to close.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not push it too far, and close the wound according to your need, then let it rest one night, as it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the tweezer.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	If the wounds of the two eyes help in the removal of the hair, and at the beginning of combing, and for many diseases, and empetigines, and corrosions, and herpes, and estiomenes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and assess the quality of the health if it is that the patient strains his neck to one side or the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and if the master is standing at the side of the patient's shoulder, and the patient is lying down, then the vein is long, then draw out a little blood, as much as possible;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then draw out another part in the other vein, then separate the limbs, and strain the veins gently, so that the patient does not suffer;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until the morning, if the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the teeth of the lips is aided in the mouth, and corruption of the genitals, and cracks in the lips, and toothache and tooth loss.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is determined if it is necessary to make the patient stand before you, and tighten their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the eye, and look at them, of which one is on the left and the other on the right, and they are identified by their blackness, and by the fact that they have thin black lines.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Check one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then check the largest of each part, and do the same for all the eyes that are similar, because it is a different way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healthy tongue, the language
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins that are open and long if helped after the healing of the head, and it is to the throat's scarcity, and there are diseases of the eyes, and there are diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the health if it is that the patient suffers when the medicine is placed between one's hands in front of the sun, and the tongue is made to lie, and looks at each side of a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	and the health is cured, and do not let it be too much, for it is the veins.

et soit li flaimes anesil.	and the old scars should be considered.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot remove it, then put your hand in cold water, and let the wound dry well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the pain worsens the first time, but returns in a second pore, because the lesion is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and I will make a poultice of the other ankle.
