Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pain in the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the foot, and its cure is the pain in the knee, when it is full of blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its health if it is that the patient enters or bathes, and strains the ankle IV times in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, if the healthy person is in all ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is worth copying if the patient is well, for the leech is safe, and it is replied to by human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not copy, if the healthy person has no one who opens or does not open, and goes to the small toe, and you wear out the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make so much evacuation of blood that you see, and then let go of the ligament, and put on cotton and strain.
ele est maintenant sanee.	The patient is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of causes of birth
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum pumps are made of horn, or iron, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and vacuum is created in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this vacuum is created by cutting in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is at full heat, or by heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the vacuum created by cutting and extracting blood is made in twelve hours of the sun's course, with some being all at once.
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the other is left in place.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And two more in the other cheek.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the suction of the mouth;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the suction of the other two shoulder blades;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction of the groins;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the suctions of the inside of the arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the suctions of the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the suctions of the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And the suction does not treat any blood, for it is scattered throughout the body, and therefore there are no veins that are not affected, as we do with wounds;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And only then is it necessary that she be anesthetized, without any fire or sensation of fire, in no disease that comes from overload, as long as the heart is dry;
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessary for diseases, or due to habits, if the midwife attends every hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and also in every ten;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have to assist at childbirth, have heavy heads.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if there are those who, when they are full and have a fever in their face, in their head, and in their neck, and are pale;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who have a chill in their mouth, their tongue has swollen, and they spit out blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are those who feel weak, see signs of fever, cold, and other symptoms.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we saw these signs, and at the same time when the month was over, we commanded them to fast for three hours after noon.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The patient with the infected eye seeks help for the pain caused by the eyes watering and the swelling... only after all the pus has been drained.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	If the ventilation is in the head of the infected eye, and it is only used by those with a cold complexion or those who have been crying, as this can cause significant harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Therefore, only the watchman should use ventilation, and those who have or are suffering from head colds.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often get better, if they become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to put the ventouse a little further down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the neck of the infected eye and the base of the skull is used for relief from pain, and to reduce swelling, redness, and inflammation.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The patient is instructed to bind it loosely, as it tends to tighten too much and cause discomfort in the stomach or chest and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The patient suffers from chest pain and shortness of breath, which worsens with exertion, causing the heart to palpitate and the jaw to ache, and leading to toothaches. It is an indication of the disease of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is recommended that you instruct the patient to express his hand when putting on the bandage, so as not to cut the artery and cause hemorrhaging.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The patient experiences pain in the neck if it is caused by a disease of the mouth, oral corruption, and similar diseases that affect the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is in the gums of the second lower lip.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from chlor and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventricles of the throat are worth as much as the third veins of the arms, for it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And command the patient not to do too much, for his lung is empty of air and knows how to compress and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The ventilator that is in the chest is worth as much as the foundation of the body, and has diseases, and it must be large and deep, with a good ability to breathe.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it is too subtle, it will break.
et i fai grans plaies.	I cause great pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The abdominal pounds are healthy when they open widely, for they attract blood from the entire body, and alleviate old pain from menstruation, childbirth, and bladder issues, and relax the muscles.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	They are in the legs of the II soles and the II heels, and they make the body weak after long use, and cause pain in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to set the abdominal pound is to first empty it, and then continue until you see the redness and swelling, and the appearance of the bruise.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, firmly place the forceps, and prepare in the position of the corsets, as some have such large shoulders and narrow chests.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is recommended to wound once only, and make wide cuts, and a small amount.
et suce legierement.	and gently lick.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not thin, if it is wounded twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time by making the vein thinner for the large amount of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is not very swift, if it is wounded a third time:
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out small veins frequently, we only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish to draw blood, if we often return.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if we wish to draw blood, if we often return; and if it is not swift, then it is finished if the vein is perceived to be sore, and those who have thick skin and are hard, and who have large pores, you should cleanse the handles of the oily, dissolving lamps.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this manner, of olive oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of the seed oil of cucumber.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in this way, of ivy oil, or of lily oil, or of chamomile, or other such likeness.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take warm oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and apply it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is dry and large pores, it is not recommended to apply oil, but it is recommended to wash after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or violet water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if the mouth is dry, if it rises from honey, or rose water, and summer, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive abundance rise from wine vials, or of ague of ailments, or of decoction of anet or of chamomile, or of other such things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And they do not become more healthier by ventouche before the bath but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And they do not sleep much after ventouche, and they become weary when they should be ventouched and when they are ventouched;
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And if those who are healthy are cooled, and if without them they are too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it happens that they crave cold things, such as pomes grenates and endives and laitues at the dairy, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And remove pus, and charred flesh, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, if they suck honey syrup and sweet wine that is between wet and dry, and remove pus and small pieces of skin and pimples, and
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when it starts to rain, if it must drink more than water.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men no time of trial or massage before the wind, or afterwards, to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And make them subtle, but only those who are thirsty should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	1. The instruments that are put in to cause pain are those that are put into the liver, and the stomach, and gout, and the intestines and bowels and veins and bones, for this member does not suffer from external injury, and it is only caused by drawing blood from one part to another, as we do with the breasts when they are sick.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	2. to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we do with the breasts when we take out the abscess from the belly and the bowels to relieve the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	3. and to relieve the pain, when it is inflamed or pierced, if it is relieved by its own virtue attracting the inflammation, or if the piercing is separated from its limb.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	When the patient is placed on the stomach and the chest, and when it has been retained, these ventouses are administered empty by sucking only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And never have been administered hot fire, and never plained of cold decoction, as in such diseases that cause pains, and in this manner we fill the ventouse with warm water, or with cold water if it has been cooked with useful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half palm of the hand, and it has one cost on the little puss, as if to poke an aguille, and it is of wax, so that it does not stick to the patient's member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in a certain environment, there is a way across iron or steel, using a wedge, and these are both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the umbilical cords of children are not like thicknesses, and neither are they fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one insert this umbilical cord into the member?
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the wedge of clay or grease, and insert the umbilical cord through the hole of the wedge that has been inserted into the wedge, so that it is clear at the end of the wedge and does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then it is placed on the member, and your wounds must be seen if we have said, so that if you see, if there is fever, and if you ventilate.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Then apply the liniment as before, and often resume it, if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventilated room, which is for the treatment of coughs and colds, there is no fever or cough, and it is not infected only when it is plain with a cold, and it is placed on the member only so much.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Wounds are not infected only when they are in the limbs where it is not possible to ventilate due to their small size, like the lips and genitals, and they look like these.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in the case of dislocation, if it is not treated promptly, and other similar cases.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the user if it is that without water that are in soft drinks, if they are taken;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And they are given a nut in soft water, as long as they are not pregnant, and have no children in the belly;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then it is cleaned and dried, and then the limb is washed as much as it is red, and the wounds are dressed;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they will be flat and smooth, if it is the joint or can be dressed, it is put in, because this is after;
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the leg of ease, and then of pain, well, and then stretch it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if it feels too tight after the corset of the stays, if I am cold and wet, and put on, as long as they are not stretched.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the stays are multiplied, if you put on vitrol or gas, and similar things, as long as they are stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or if you put on the leg half of picked walnuts, and leave them as they cool to the leg, it will now stretch.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more of these, if you take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	If the wounds do not take on the salve, if you rub the wound with warm oil or insert a needle as much as it does not hurt, and then put it on, and as they feel the heat, if they burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are smarting, if you sprinkle on a little aloe and silk, or charcoal, they will now burn.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	2. This is the beginning of the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	3. These cauteries are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are a restoration of wounds and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Tell them, that the leaf will make the patient's skin smart from this chapter, that they will never see any of the old books, nor letter will come out.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the science is neglected in our land, because I have never found any book.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and no one knows otherwise, for it is by the science of ancient books, or because I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and condensed at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the strangulations that are mistaken, as I have done in these two previous chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	1. It is therefore necessary that we say the introduction of this book, the words and chapters, and the surgeons understand their meaning, and they should pay attention to the truth, so that those who have experienced it and learned this noble art can teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, or twisting occurs in no way, if you must first heal the patient on one side and the other, nothing else can help, just like how it is with wounds, or tumors, or galls.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If the joint is not very tense, or too loose.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	If the joint is too loose, it is known as cold joints, and should not contain any fatty tissue, no thin charcuterie, and no excessive consumption of meat that fills the veins with blood, until you do not doubt aposteme chaut, nor expansion of matter in the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient's condition improves after using the treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's meat that causes great swelling, or if it has viscosity, like wheat cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made of wool, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling decreases and the fracture is less soon.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And you know that bones broken by fractures and decrepitude cannot be well restored or surged according to their nature by the care of the members, nor those who are too soft, like small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But there is no cure, first reset the broken bone and large fragments that are pulled out and join the limb together as much as possible, just as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not pull too hard on its work, and because it causes great pain from large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	The treatise explains that there are various types of fractures, each with its own characteristics and causes.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	However, the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will explain all types of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that occur when falling, and others that result from being struck, similar to the size of a quill used for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	If a fracture is accompanied by a wound, it can be a small cut or nick.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to have his engine and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes to his memory in his head.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known the bone fracture by what causes it to be twisted, and wide open by defense, and some by pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when it is not twisted and does not touch the toes, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have knots, or roughness, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it with your hand alone, but apply the medicine that comes after, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you suspect that the fracture will occur in the fall, and the two parts of the bone are separated, it is now necessary to align them as evenly as possible, without causing further injury.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the bone is set, and it does not cause any pain, as long as the pain is eased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then you should align it gently and carefully, and suspect that the restoration of the bone is lighter than the restorations of other bones or if there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And then hold it steady until it is done.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	When there are broken pieces in the bone, if it is two parts, it is hands or foot, or in your hand it is some small limbs, or in the cords, or in one cord and in your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member in its natural position, if by the parts of the broken member they are out of place, then reset them with your fingers in the joint that you see, and make sure that by your effort there is no injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two heads of the bones as well as the best forms;
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And it feels good in the hand if it seems that it is not well done:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the swelling improves nicely and is not strained too much, do not press as hard as those who cause it to come out through their abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is swollen, if the patient is careful not to move it too much, neither during the day nor at night, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And be well that the limb is firmly bandaged to ensure that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if there is no pain, and it is not swollen, then it is necessary to put on clothing that does not cause any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight, so that twisting does not come when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is known that the broken member can be different in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For it has many limbs, just like fingers and toes, and similar ones.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	if it is covered with flax and wool of a fineness and subtlety such as.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are thick, just like a knot and a leg.
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if they are covered with a thick and hard linen, because the large linens wrap around the whole limb, and they are drawn equally from all parts, if it has no tension.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then the hand is lightly tourniqueted with three or four turns around the member, and the hand is stretched a little for the entire length, then it goes to the end of the fracture and is stretched less than the fracture, which the fracture slightly moves away from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and softens the ligament a little and a little, as you grip a large part of the healthy member, then take another ligament, and turn it rightwise over the broken member;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the part opposite the fracture, and stretch it gently, not too much nor too little, as we have said in the first lesson;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then insert the threads between the stitched lines of linen or drapery, as it is even, then tie them with silk and braid, and then put your well-made eyes on them, if there is no slippage or fraying.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is fraying or slippage, then put something calming for slippage on it, and that stops the fraying, and leaves no uneven parts.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tighten your eyes, and be of one and a half inch wide, rough hemp, or fust that is used for nails, or rings of palm, and be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the piece that is placed on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should also be long enough to fit the member of small or large size.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then pull on the strings as you did in the first session, then tie a thread around it, just like in the first session.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The more it is stretched, the less it is.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the thread be clean, not too thick nor too thin, and be made of linen thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	Because if the thread is too thick, it is like the works of the foxes who make their lashings of linen threads, and it is a great mistake, for the lashing cannot be equal if it is too fine, and only serves to have less space between each string.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is dislocated due to the hairs of the eyelids after plucking them in good health, if they make holes in the skin, or cause inflammation, if it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the forceps, and the nail is broken, I will tell you the cure for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And he should not try to straighten all the broken limbs at once.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not proper to put on tight clothes that will afterwards cause pain after six or seven days, or according to your aposteme's strength.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And then the way of ancient plasters to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And is that you make a dough that holds within the walls of the mill, and knead with much beer, and make this confection, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore breaks in other positions, and even women and children, for it is not too hard or too wet.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Prepare a mixture of oak bark, linseed oil, and Arabic gum, and mulat; mix it with X parts of water.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mince the ingredients and aloe, mix it with X parts of water.
alechil VIIII З.;	Add aleochil in the mixture, X parts of water.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	Then make a powder, and mix with pork fat.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the skull is hot, then use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Other method of plaster that is used:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mud and mix it with water, then let it dry for about 12 hours.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	grind and add aloe, then let it dry for about 79 hours.
acaice VI З.;	mix with ice for about 6 minutes.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	mix with arsenic (armenicum) for about 10 minutes, then boil well and cook with water or urine, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and bones is to take the bones out of their sockets, soothe the pain, and make them fit, and the fractures heal.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new gauze, mix it with oil and cooked butter, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	2. These plasters do not repair anything, but they are useful for soothing abscesses and properly addressing bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to fracture that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Use dried figs, and dry earth pottery, break them together, and make a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	4. Another plaster to repair the bone fracture and to help heal the abscess: take dried fig leaves and earth oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Use the root of valerian, chamomile, violets, flour of wheat, of each a part.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and boil, and mix with wine, and when the members are washed, mix with fresh coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster more forcefully than the first, when an abscess is coming out of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Use the roots of valerian, linseed, honey, honey, and violets and chamomile, of each a part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And cut, and bind with saltwater, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that no material is used to set a broken bone for restoration, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It appears that Galien suggests that when setting a broken bone for restoration, one should use dry things like cheese, mirrory aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to detect injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take raw and cooked oats, or wool from sheep, and glue, and cut them evenly, and bind, and then apply it and hold it in place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then take a pouch afterward, and keep an eye on the patient's pain does not feel any pain, and does not move the bones of his arm.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not taken by hand.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	If pain comes to the limb, or itching, if you touch it, and it swells, and now the plaster is loose.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and gently loosen it, and use wet seawater, and dip in cool water, and raise the swollen limb as much as the itching stops, and soothe the pain.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then rest the limb for an hour, then put on a dry bandage, smooth with water or olive oil, and tie tightly until you are sure there is no sign of gangrene.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the swollen limb, and soothe the pain, then resume gently tying with a small piece of plaster, and a little emplasater, and do not strain it too much.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And gently as long as it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the wound is bleeding, swollen, painful, and inflamed, and you have the skill to plaster and bandage, if it recurs, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the member that we have said, if it does not slip after three days or four or seven or ten.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And never leaves it for twenty days, according to what we see, as long as the fracture is healing, and approaches the joint of the cart.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	However, the restraint is more than the first, and its flesh increases as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the shoulder drying more than it should, screams that no one can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The first line of the text translates to: "When the fever rises, you must wash your face several times a day, regardless of the time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	The second line translates to: "By this means, the swelling in the member is reduced, and the pain subsides, restoring the member to its natural state.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	The third line translates to: "This is unfortunate, and if it persists, I can only recommend rest and proper care.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounding
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	The fourth line translates to: "There are many types of wounds, and various shapes, and the causes are different.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	The fifth line translates to: "For there are wounds made by the impact of a spear, and they pierce the entire bone, just like a thorn or a nail.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For this reason, it is called this method of fracture "hair-cutting".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	The speckled bone is cut through by various senses, and this method of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound from these two great or small fractures is.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is made by a thrust that is embedded, or cut, or by the edge of a pierce, or by the point after a pierce, or by other such means.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent wound, which approaches the skin that is exposed to the bone, or it is under the bone, and this is the injury or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is repaired in the bone is as fine as some needles, and is a small cut, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound that is made by cutting with a sharp object, or by piercing, or by some other means, and causes the piece of bone to enter, and it is called the "hotter" when they heat the hotters;
si entre li piere dedens.	If it enters the wound.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And there are more who have moist hair, like children's hair.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and come in all these ways of fracture that are lightly cut if like these;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak to it in its own language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let's examine all the ways of fractures by the methods used, and by the corrupted char that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and rubs it with a cloth, if the dark fracture is not wide open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close eye on the patient's condition, and if you see no serious complications, such as vomiting, confusion, apathy, muscle relaxation, fever, and redness, and other symptoms that cannot be cured, seek medical attention.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you expect a cure to begin.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the bone comes first to you, and it is in your hand, if it is necessary to cut the bone before the fortieth day, then you must.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, if you have cut the bone before the ninth day, then the wound that we have mentioned will be corrupted and the accident will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes near the edge of the skin that the scar hides, then you must cut off the damaged part.
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if you burn the patient's hair as it grows, and cut along the bone in all ways you can, and along the shape of the wound more so than you can, and to reveal the bone, or to expose the muscle, and if you help with this that you can, and then fill the wound with oily powdered flax.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest as long as the inflammation is eased, and be assured of its correlation with blood.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then the bone begins to erode, and it is done according to two methods of incision:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is when you cut at the narrowed end, and it is formed like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then, a larger piece is cut than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is when you have many different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and you perform them lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and thick, then you must perforate it from the inside, otherwise, you should make holes with smaller drills, and do not let the point go further into the bone, and it must have a margin or a circle that does not allow the point to go further into the bone:
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you should have more of them if many people have this condition when their bone grows in their shoulder, if you have tried everything for your test.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And it is the form of the three ways of trying:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality of piercing into the broken bone is that you put one try on the bone and turn it as much as you can until you feel that the bone is perceived.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then I put the try on another part of the bone, and then I do everything, then cut as much as you can with the incisors of the bone that is between the plugs, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as long as you draw the bone from your hand, or from any of the splints that you have like nails, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and keep your hands away from the skull and the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	When you perceive the bone, and treat it, if you cover that the worn-out plate of the bone with another instrument resembling an incisor, but it should be more fine and delicate than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there is no wear on the small bones, neither any scales, if the light bones are slightly affected by the strains.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound and injuries that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of treating it is what the Gaulish doctors say, which is more certain.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the loud one, very much so, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and bleeding. Once you have removed this part, measure from the edge of this incisional lenticular loop, of which the shape is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut too much of one part, and the other part becomes in two pieces, so that when it is cut, it is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then, with a small tool, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and you will be well prepared for the cloth that is loose.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is near the bone, if you lightly touch the bone, because one touches the bone painfully and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissues, and it has small pieces, if they cover that roughness, and smooth the scales with a subtle rasping tool that you must have several quantities of, to adapt each limb to its use according to the type and position of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave in front of a coarse rasping tool, and then switch to a softer one, and continue doing this as much as it is necessary.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In every other small incision and subtle break, it is necessary to amputate according to his address.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And that is something that cannot be answered by the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scar is discovered, then it is necessary to apply oil on linen according to the size of the wound, and the ointment is put on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another doubled strip of linen, and the ointment in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first strip.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you please, so as not to worsen the scar, then apply with another piece of linen, and do not strain it too much, only as it will tag the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And let it stay in the bed for one or two days, until the inflammation is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as roots of various kinds, flour, and powdered incense, and Aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make powder from these things and place it on the wound, and administer further medications without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is clean, do not apply ointment, and do not gather bows, because when bows are assembled on the skin, they often cause great pain to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when something biting is placed on the skin, it may cause harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents come to the patient, if no one doubts, as we have said, if there is any doubt in sense.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no color comes forth but through medicine we have put on, which has some virtue, then it is necessary to apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one part of glue, and then place it on the skin.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment is in various ways that cover the wounds, as long as they are healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Scars that have never been broken in the two parts of the skin, or only one, are because they are bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that is cartilaginous, and does not break easily, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off the small toe or nail and make the break as equal as possible on your index finger, and in the pocket until it matches its natural figure.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the middle of the nail and cannot be reached by the thumb, then you must place it evenly at the tip of a large pocket.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, then you should redo it, and hurry to restore the first joint, if possible.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if this is not possible, then after the ninth or tenth day, when the wound has stopped bleeding, cut off the small toe and nail, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you cut one part, the other will also break.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and if they are too large, they fill the abscesses with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restaurer will say that one must smooth the wounds with a blade, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems to me that this is the best, but they should be made in the composition of mull, and oatmeal powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the dressing, until the bone is firm and the cartilage becomes hard.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And no time is lost in putting sheep's gut in the wounds, and if the skin is loose and hangs down, and holds tightly, and smells the salves among.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to the eye while you are working, if it is made of wool or cotton that has been greased with oil of rosemary, or in a pot of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not heal, apply plaster made from flour of sisal, incense powder, and lamb's wool ashes, then place soft sponges on it, and do not tie it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the wound is small and it is torn into thin pieces, and the tearing is done with suitable instruments, then cauterize, and treat the surrounding things as charred, and swearing, if burning and cauterizing are suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound or small wound, and the patient is cured by tenting, and puts on bandages, as soon as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is slight only, and not in two pieces, but rather a thin crack, which can be felt, if one knows how to do it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the left side, that you bind your index finger in the mouth of the midwife.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, then bind your index finger of the right hand with your left index finger, lightly bind the fracture, and fix it with the other hand in place.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described as a second degree, then it comes that you administer extension of two parts, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth move or break, or if they are pulled out of a gold, silver, or silk thread, then put the thread on the broken jawbone, and put two sheets over it.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the patient's head a well-made cap, or a piece of leather that is long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it to the neck that you choose, and instruct the patient to rest, and give them light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the joint changes shape, if it shifts during the night, and then return to the point where it was previously;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a poultice on it, with flour from the bolster or wheat flour, after you have applied the mustard to the head;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place the poultice on it, with a light bandage, and if it becomes wet, let it dry completely before changing the dressing, as long as it remains healthy;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	The patient's condition improves after three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the wound becomes inflamed, then we have said many times what to do about it.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	If there is a fracture and wound combined, the piece of bone in the joint is reduced.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the bone has subtle projections that are flexible to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the pieces of bone, and there is no need for them, if the wound is wide, and place them in removable dressings as needed, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways.
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it is broken and displaced in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operation is when the fracture is near the wound, if you have two assistants, so that one marks the helper who feels the force of the fracture.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and he extends the other arm towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the incision at your own side, as it should be, and make sure there are no appearances or movements.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you must extend further, then place the shoulder of the patient against a round object made of linen or wool, and make it as large as necessary.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold and gently apply the force, and pull the bead towards your hand, so that you can place the incision at the same point as before.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you do not treat the head of the force with care, because it comes in front, and the patient may fall on his face or head, and place the shoulder outside the eye socket, and support the shoulder with your hand until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then close the incision at your own side, and if you break the limb, then it is necessary to amputate.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And then cut through the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, if it is one of the incisions you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but if you use too much force on this instrument, to avoid damaging the face:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, and is not too thin, and should be as wide as the bone desires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the will:
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, if you see, and the larger ones are for wider pieces, and the smaller ones are for narrower pieces, according to the swelling of the wound you made when you treated the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	When you are sure of the incision, if the wound is small, and if the burn is not large, or if you doubt the incision, if the wound is made of linen and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if blood comes out of the wound, then pour oil on it, rosewater, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The softening of the bone is when it has pains and is feeling small, you should then put on the bone a poultice made of flour and urine powder, and light sponges, and a spike of wool at the end, if you have the skill.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage of a palm leaf, then put on a double fold of sponges, and apply it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin needle of III dozen wide and long, and wrap it around the bend, so that the end of the bend is secure.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the needle on the bridge, turn the bend around the neck, and take out the healthy shoe, and take out the sick shoe.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bone holds the bridge firmly, and you clearly see that the needle does not move from the broken bone, then reward each one accordingly, and when the joint is loose, then the constraint.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie down on his back, and when he falls asleep, put a small pillow under his head, to lift the helper to the top.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the fracture is aligned by aligning the shoulder or tying the arm to the collarbone, and it does not dislocate due to accidents, it should be able to hold for about 20 years.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then continue the splinting, if you see that it has its use, and tighten and release it as needed until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it will be restored in about 28 years, with no harm to anyone.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Only the shoulder bone breaks or becomes loose in the body and does not move on its own, and it does not occur unless touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the limb appears distorted, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put powdered sulfur with much urine on the limb, and lightly sprinkle it, and make a double loop.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put a wide and thin plate, a bit larger than the shoulder blade, on the limb, and if it is not well adjusted, use a woolen bandage for adjustment.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then tie it tightly with a long iron band, so that the plate does not move from its place, and watch the line every hour.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it is dislocated, if it is pulled, and sets the joint at its place, and the patient feels pain on their chest;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the spine is restored in XX days or XXV.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if it does not return, and be sure, because this is only what makes the joint feel lighter.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone is found before the other, and there is no sound when it is struck, then it is said that the bone has been fractured, and we make the repair as we have described in the reduction of the force of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the bone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is never broken in its environment, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the joint.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the environment, if it is out of place, and there is great pain, and loss of strength, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and opening the wounds in the broken bones, and they feel better.
